In this case, Rick is absolutely correct: The Gorget is made of nickel-silver, invented by Maillot and Chorier, around 1820. In the Anglosphere, we call it 'nickel-silver', because it's the nickel in the alloy that allows it to take a good polish. At one time, it was called German silver in the UK, probably due to discrimination of German products. ('Jerry-built' is another pejorative term).

that gorget necklace looks like a reenactor's piece. there is a fairly large community of fur trade reenactors that try to recreate historic accessories using as many actual authentic pieces as possible. the beads look old enough to be authentic and then they could be attached to a more modern made gorget (there are traditional blacksmiths and silversmiths in this community too). even if the whole thing was completely authentic though, it wouldn't sell for 100k without some kind of documented proof that it belonged to someone of note from that time period. modern made pieces aged to look authentic are quite common and are often used or made by reenactors, but passing them off as authentic to sell is definitely not encouraged or supported. also there is a big market for native american items and unfortunately there is a lot of fraud as well.

I collect antique Chinese porcelain, and I remember I used to frequent a very friendly site where we would swap images and info. But there was this one guy who kept claiming that he had multiple pieces of ruyi porcelain. If you don't know, ruyi is the very finest form of Chinese porcelain, maybe eight hundred years old, delicate and grey with a crackle pattern in it called "cicada wings". It is so rare that NOT A SINGLE INTACT PIECE has ever been found - museums are obliged to display broken ones, which are worth unimaginable amounts. I believe at latest count about fourteen such broken pieces survive.  This guy claimed he had multiple INTACT pieces of original ruyi porcelain. He then proceeded to show image after image of horrid looking clumsy dishes with snot green glaze. It was like a sinusitis patient sneezed on the fishpond decorations in a garden centre.  No matter what we said, this person refused to believe that they were NOT ruyi dishes. No doubt this was partly because he had paid a great deal for them. The worst part was that this guy clearly had no day job; so our objections were rapidly overwhelmed by hundreds and hundreds of posts by this guy defending his position. And he never stopped. No doubt he is still posting there today, eight years later. He reminds me of some of these folks  :-D.

He was paid $18 and Scotty & Bill were paid $12 per show. My Grandmother was a HUGE Elvis fan and would tell us stories about The Louisiana Hayride and Elvis. Other than Las Vegas, Shreveport has to be one of the cities that he played more shows in than any other city. And because my Grandmother and Mother were such HUGE fans, they ruined my sisters 10th Birthday party which is on August 16. And of course everyone here but the sweet old lady were the kind that even when they accepted an appraisal did not know the number one rule of pawn shops: the appraisal is a suggestion for them to sell it for and they need to make an offer. A $15,000 appraisal does NOT mean the appraiser is tell you that's the minimum for you to aim for, its the maximum for the pawn shop. Also people selling collectors items: find and online community and offer it there. The other reason pawn shops lowball you is because they can't be promised someone looking for that is going to walk in. You can guarantee the right people get it with a little effort and no middle man!
